  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_1e314aca-2875-4237-8b29-8cc717c53e7d'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

Among them: <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[beloved grandmother in a coma; grandmother was a victim of spousal abuse; heroine is a widow and also suffered a miscarriage; she falls in love with a guy who turns out to have an inoperable brain tumor. <div id="review_1533113661" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1533113661" />
    <a title="Deb" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5276322-deb"><img alt="Deb" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1526245087p2/5276322.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1533113661?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deb" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deb" href="/user/show/5276322-deb">Deb</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781586216320" href="/book/show/21447.Sam_s_Letters_to_Jennifer">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1533113661" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16557564654667857085"><i>
  <b>Sam's Letters to Jennifer is heartwarming and bittersweet.</b>
</i><br/><br/>This book definitely gave me more than I expected. The cover, so <i>Nicholas Sparks</i>-ish did not lure me in. Actually it made me question was this a book I really wanted to read. The bittersweet sappy theme usually doesn't draw me in. It usually pushes me away. Too nice sometimes is too boring. There's a repetitive formula to these types of books that I have a hard time buying. But I said why not and decided to give it a try. I assumed it</span>
  <span id="freeText16557564654667857085" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>Sam's Letters to Jennifer is heartwarming and bittersweet.</b>
</i><br /><br />This book definitely gave me more than I expected. The cover, so <i>Nicholas Sparks</i>-ish did not lure me in. Actually it made me question was this a book I really wanted to read. The bittersweet sappy theme usually doesn't draw me in. It usually pushes me away. Too nice sometimes is too boring. There's a repetitive formula to these types of books that I have a hard time buying. But I said why not and decided to give it a try. I assumed it would be a woman reading letters from some long lost love but this story was not about that at all. <br /><br />You see, Sam, is short for Samantha. Sam is Jennifer's grandmother. Jennifer, her widowed granddaughter is called to town because her grandmother is in the hospital in a coma. Jennifer goes to her grandmothers house and finds stacks of letters that her grandmother wrote to her telling her about her life. The first letter begins with a shocking revelation that motivates Jennifer to continue to read all the letters in hopes of learning her grandmothers secrets. While staying at her grandmothers house Jennifer romantically reunites with a childhood friend, Brendan who has a secret of his own. <br /><br />My thoughts on this book are a little on the fence. On the one hand I'm glad that though certain characters received a second chance at love. Whether it is opening ones self back up to love after grief or love after a bad relationship, there's nothing like being given the opportunity to share in a healthy real love. This is good. On the other hand I don't necessarily agree with the glorification or offhanded romanticism of the extramarital affair. If the relationship was abusive, leave and go be with the new guy but I just found the affair too condoning and romanticized. Even if the bad husband is bad it doesn't make it valid. I did like the parallel between the relationship that was lost to death and how a second chance was given. That was nice. <br /><br />I'll give this book a 3 1/2 stars. It was surprisingly a good story. I'd recommend it. I may read other books by this author. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16557564654667857085" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer16726761" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12327372717137369294">The story of a grown woman who feels she has lost everything in her life. her best friend; her grandmother just fell into a coma while the love of her life died a couple years back, partly because it was her fault. She spends restless days within the shadow of blame and regret towards herself while the anouncment of her grandmothers condition is discovered. The grandmother, sam, has left her letters in order to let her understand things in her life that no one else has. She begins to understand </span>
  <span id="freeText12327372717137369294" style="display:none">The story of a grown woman who feels she has lost everything in her life. her best friend; her grandmother just fell into a coma while the love of her life died a couple years back, partly because it was her fault. She spends restless days within the shadow of blame and regret towards herself while the anouncment of her grandmothers condition is discovered. The grandmother, sam, has left her letters in order to let her understand things in her life that no one else has. She begins to understand how sam and her are very similar especailly on how they had given up on love. While sam describes her story, jennifer meets a man from her past and....well the story continues from there.<br /><br />I loved the book. it was extremely hooking and draws you into this vivid image of the setting and all the events. it was as if you felt what the characters were feeling and James Patterson did an amazing job on that. I cried at the random moments even though the plot is close to that of a cliche. It's something that seems to have derived from an oscar winning movie and if it doesnt become one, i'd be extremely disappointed. Reminds me of the notebook because of the similarites although they have 2 very different morals, plots etc. I learned that if you want happiness, you shouldnt shut out things in your life that make you happy. You shouldnt give up on life and love even if you hit rock bottom. I recommend this book to those who love reading about romance, or simply the relationships between individuals.</span>

<div id="review_2298228652" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Katherine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13311251-katherine"><img alt="Katherine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577842427p2/13311251.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780316710572" href="/book/show/1015020.Sam_s_Letters_to_Jennifer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=bloody-awful">bloody-awful</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=dishonor-on-your-cow">dishonor-on-your-cow</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=instalove-express">instalove-express</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=love-triangle">love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=baa-baa-black-sheep">baa-baa-black-sheep</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2298228652" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9144151477542140600"><b>
  <i>”Please don’t shut out love- it’s the best thing about life.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>The world works in mysterious ways, friends. And I believe in that saying now more than ever.<br/><br/>I say this because I do not understand how any agent, editor, or publisher would allow such an abominably written book to be published. <br/><br/>Jennifer has always had a close relationship with her grandmother, Sam. So, when Sam falls into a coma after a freak accident, Jennifer rushes to be by her side. While there she discovers a bundle of letter</span>
  <span id="freeText9144151477542140600" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>”Please don’t shut out love- it’s the best thing about life.”</i>
</b><br /><br />The world works in mysterious ways, friends. And I believe in that saying now more than ever.<br /><br />I say this because I do not understand how any agent, editor, or publisher would allow such an abominably written book to be published. <br /><br />Jennifer has always had a close relationship with her grandmother, Sam. So, when Sam falls into a coma after a freak accident, Jennifer rushes to be by her side. While there she discovers a bundle of letters that Sam had written to her about her life and a few little secrets she’s been keeping from everyone. While reading those letters, Jennifer begins to discover a while new side to her grandmother and gains a whole new lease on life, which entails learning to love again after her husband passes away. <br /><br />A friend described this book as ‘trashtastic’ and at first, I disagreed with her. I wasn’t expecting quality literature with this book. I was just expecting a nice, sweet love story to fly through as a quick, mindless read. And in the beginning, that’s what I got; a nice sweet story.<br /><br />But then apparently the author’s editor decided to take a vacation or not work for Patterson or something, because the writing was absolutely atrocious. Extremely bad. My seven-year-old niece could write a book better than this. How on earth, I wondered to myself, could this book have been written by James Patterson? Isn’t he supposed to be this famous, best-selling author who has been around a while and written about a gazillion books? If that’s the case, shouldn’t his writing be better than this? The writing was so bad that it made my eyes roll into the back of my head. If I had to proofread the entire book with a red pen in hand, the pages would be so red George R.R. Martin would have to write The Red Wedding, 2.0. Grammar wise and punctuation wise, this book was awful.<br /><br />But wait; it gets better. Because it’s not just the basic grammar and punctuation that’s bad; the entire plot of the book feels incomplete. This may have something to do with the fact that there are so many plot holes in this book that it looks like a slice of Swiss cheese. For instance, we know that Jennifer’s husband passes away, and Patterson tells us when and where. But he doesn’t tell us why. He just goes to Hawaii and then, poof! He’s gone. What happened to him? Did he drown in the ocean? Get eaten by a shark? Fall into an erupting volcano? <b>WHAT HAPPENED??!!</b> Patterson does this a lot; he vaguely writes about tragic events that happen, but never fleshes them out in detail. I mean, I know we as readers aren’t stupid, but the whole fade to black approach isn’t that great either. <br /><br />The entire plot of the book was more akin to a Lifetime or Hallmark movie than an actual book. Everything moved rather fast with little to no answers provided to the reader. The plot is pretty simplistic, which makes it a mindless read, but when it’s coupled with the fact that it’s cheesy as hell; well, it makes for a torturous read. Some professional reviewers compared this book to Nicholas Sparks’ writing, but that would be an insult to Nicholas Sparks himself. I never thought I would say this, considering how famous (and infamous) Sparks is, but his novels are far superior than this book ever hopes to be. <br /><br />Look, there’s just no nice way to put it; this book was awful. It was so bad I can’t really quite wrap my head around the fact that this book got published. By a major publishing house. It managed to go through the rounds of editors, agents, and general goddamn proofreaders and it STILL, somehow, managed to be published. Not only that, it was one of the top 10 published best-selling books the year it was published. I will never be able to explain how, since the writing is atrocious, the dialogue laughable, and the entire plot missing so many key points that it’ll probably fall into a black hole. Patterson usually writes books with a co-writer and let me tell you; I hope they’re better than this book. Because so far, Patterson solo is a complete and utter disaster.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9144151477542140600" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Rachel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3107864-rachel"><img alt="Rachel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1324006058p2/3107864.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/119017566?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel" href="/user/show/3107864-rachel">Rachel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3107864-rachel?shelf=2010">2010</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer119017566" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18368834922480412947">There is something about a guilty pleasure book -- a quick read that is entirely predictable but still tugs at your heartstrings. This is how I would classify <i>Sam's Letters to Jennifer.</i><br/><br/>I was a bit skeptical about reading this book, considering I had read <i>Sundays at Tiffany's</i> earlier this year and was wasn't too impressed with it. But, the dust jacket intrigued me, and I could tell it'd be a quick read like <i>Sundays at Tiffany's</i>, so I gave it a shot.<br/><br/>Being a Minnesotan, I really enjoyed how the boo</span>
  <span id="freeText18368834922480412947" style="display:none">There is something about a guilty pleasure book -- a quick read that is entirely predictable but still tugs at your heartstrings. This is how I would classify <i>Sam's Letters to Jennifer.</i><br /><br />I was a bit skeptical about reading this book, considering I had read <i>Sundays at Tiffany's</i> earlier this year and was wasn't too impressed with it. But, the dust jacket intrigued me, and I could tell it'd be a quick read like <i>Sundays at Tiffany's</i>, so I gave it a shot.<br /><br />Being a Minnesotan, I really enjoyed how the book was set in the Midwest. In a culture where all of us either own a lake home or know someone who does, having a majority of the book take place in Lake Geneva was a real treat, especially since I read it in the last days of summer.<br /><br />While a simple book, Patterson does a good job of establishing strong bonds between Jennifer and her grandmother, Sam. Getting to know Sam's life in the midst of Jennifer dealing with her own after much heartache was enjoyable, light reading.<br /><br />Of course, a guilty pleasure book like this can't be without its predictability: tragedy causing main characters to not open up immediately, love developing between childhood friends, and a baby being the ultimate symbol of true love. Sometimes, though, it's not so bad reading the formulaic cheesiness. After all, most people want to believe that no matter what kind of troubles you've had in your life thus far, you are still capable of falling in love and living happily ever after. In this book, Patterson keeps that dream alive.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18368834922480412947" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10719500763234137766">Jennifer was summoned back to her hometown where she was raised by her grandmother. Her grandmother Samantha, took very ill with a heart attack and is in a coma in the hospital.<br/><br/>When Jennifer arrives home there, she discovers a pack of letters which have been addressed specifically to her by Sam.   <span id="freeText10719500763234137766" style="display:none">Jennifer was summoned back to her hometown where she was raised by her grandmother. Her grandmother Samantha, took very ill with a heart attack and is in a coma in the hospital.<br /><br />When Jennifer arrives home there, she discovers a pack of letters which have been addressed specifically to her by Sam. In every letter, her grandma reveals many sad memories of her past. She speaks of her late husband Charles, who beat her over the years, and the affair she had been carrying on the side with a man, Doc, of whom she fell deeply in love. Jennifer is shocked to discover this as she reads on in her grandma's story.<br /><br />Also, she runs into Brendan, the kid she nicknamed Scout when they were kids and played together. They discover a newfound love, and have a summer romance. Jennifer doesn't realize though that Brendan, is hiding a terrible secret of his own, and is devastated when she finds out that he is very very ill.<br /><br />Her grandmother may rally, and Brendan may have a miracle operation which either cures his illness, or will make him much worse. So in the end he has to make a difficult decision; die, or maybe live a little longer.<br /><br />A wonderful novel, and one you don't lay down until the end.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4626699663598758910">If immorality and infidelity are your thing, this book is for you. The whole basis of the story is an unhappy woman who has a secret affair for years and after her husband dies, she marries him, secretly. Sam writes letters to her granddaughter, Jennifer, and details the relationship. My problem with it is that the author glamorized the relationship, like she was to be admired because she didn't leave her husband. <br/><br/>The best part of the book is this quote: "For a long time it had seemed to me that</span>
  <span id="freeText4626699663598758910" style="display:none">If immorality and infidelity are your thing, this book is for you. The whole basis of the story is an unhappy woman who has a secret affair for years and after her husband dies, she marries him, secretly. Sam writes letters to her granddaughter, Jennifer, and details the relationship. My problem with it is that the author glamorized the relationship, like she was to be admired because she didn't leave her husband. <br /><br />The best part of the book is this quote: "For a long time it had seemed to me that life was about to begin--real life. But there was always some obstacle in the way, something to be got through first, some unfinished business, time still to be served, a debt to be paid. Then life would begin. At last it dawned on me that these obstacles were my life." --Father Alfred D'Souza <br /><br />The best part wasn't even written by the author. This book was written by the same author as Sundays at Tiffany's, which I liked. Don't bother reading this book. I'm glad I bought it at a garage sale so I won't feel badly when I toss it in the trash.</span>

<div id="review_1572894003" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1572894003" />
    <a title="Kelli" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10869520-kelli"><img alt="Kelli" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457153453p2/10869520.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1572894003?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelli" href="/user/show/10869520-kelli">Kelli</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1572894003" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17476124933026147384">I happened upon this book when I needed something to read and it was readily available on overdrive. I also wanted something light and easy as I had just finished the Goldfinch and the Nightingale... and my poor heart could not handle any more weight. I probably should have researched this a little more because it was not light at all, but it was a very easy read. A classic case of judging a book by its cover, or in my case, its title. The relationship between Jennifer and Sam was beautiful. Sam</span>
  <span id="freeText17476124933026147384" style="display:none">I happened upon this book when I needed something to read and it was readily available on overdrive. I also wanted something light and easy as I had just finished the Goldfinch and the Nightingale... and my poor heart could not handle any more weight. I probably should have researched this a little more because it was not light at all, but it was a very easy read. A classic case of judging a book by its cover, or in my case, its title. The relationship between Jennifer and Sam was beautiful. Sam's letters were wonderful, sometimes sad, and full of unexpected information. This is certainly not a book that is representative of my overall taste or style, but it was pleasant enough. A solid three stars for a decent book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17476124933026147384" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_139805942" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/139805942" />
    <a title="Malerie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4735376-malerie"><img alt="Malerie" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/139805942?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Malerie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Malerie" href="/user/show/4735376-malerie">Malerie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer139805942" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3331942871405947407">I read this book because I kept hearing that it's similar to the novels of one of my favorite authors, Nicholas Sparks. However, after reading it, although I guess I can see where that comparison came to mind, I just can't bear the thought of putting this book in the same category as The Notebook and The Choice. What I appreciate about Sparks' work is that it's poetic and romantic without being pretentious or overly wordy. This was my first experience reading Patterson's work, and while the stor</span>
  <span id="freeText3331942871405947407" style="display:none">I read this book because I kept hearing that it's similar to the novels of one of my favorite authors, Nicholas Sparks. However, after reading it, although I guess I can see where that comparison came to mind, I just can't bear the thought of putting this book in the same category as The Notebook and The Choice. What I appreciate about Sparks' work is that it's poetic and romantic without being pretentious or overly wordy. This was my first experience reading Patterson's work, and while the story is quite romantic (Oh, don't let me try to fool you! I cried!), I felt like the words themselves didn't quite sit right with me at times. I hate to sound nit-picky or stuck-up, but I just have to be honest. It's not something I can quite put my finger on, but there were just times where I would be reading and think, "Hhmm....I feel like my little brother wrote that sentence." Again, it wasn't the plot itself that bothered me, just the lack of poetic beauty in the way it was sometimes told. Then again, some people may find that more relatable. Hopefully, at least ONE other person can relate to what I'm trying to say. Hahah!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3331942871405947407" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1064295995" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1064295995" />
    <a title="Hannah Phan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26841607-hannah-phan"><img alt="Hannah Phan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452286121p2/26841607.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1064295995?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1064295995" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8067100431210928699">I found this book doing the one thing you're not suppose to do with books, I was judging by the cover. <br/>I was hungry for a shameless-tear-jurking-romance novel, the story line looked right up my alley, the writer was well known and celebrated for being talented, and the cover art was pleasant. Being a big fan of Nicholas Sparks I am a seasoned veteran in wading through cliché girly mush that would make normal people vomit (and love every minute of it) Sparks novel's reduced me to sobbing quietly </span>
  <span id="freeText8067100431210928699" style="display:none">I found this book doing the one thing you're not suppose to do with books, I was judging by the cover. <br />I was hungry for a shameless-tear-jurking-romance novel, the story line looked right up my alley, the writer was well known and celebrated for being talented, and the cover art was pleasant. Being a big fan of Nicholas Sparks I am a seasoned veteran in wading through cliché girly mush that would make normal people vomit (and love every minute of it) Sparks novel's reduced me to sobbing quietly in my room over the last pages by the glow of the lamp on my nightstand, and always led to a little bit of emotional devastation at the hands of a paperback for a few weeks afterwards, but this book actually hurt me, and not in the good heartache way you want a novel like this to, it hurt me because of the many brain cells I lost to this mind numbing horrible novel. <br /><br />I bought his book used on Amazon for a penny, and I want my penny back. <br /><br />ATTNETION SPOILERS WILL TAKE PLACE FROM HERE FORWARD:<br /><br />First of all, the story about a girl rushing to the side of her sick grandmother who raised her, is a little cheap in my mind, but whatever, I can roll with it. What made me laugh throughout the story was that after Jennifer meets her little boyfriend, notice how many times she goes and sees her grandmother? Like, a handful. Maybe. That's fine, Granny the ill woman who raised you is just rotting on her death bed in a hospital, by all means go have some fun with your boyfriend. She'll wait. DUMB. <br /><br />Two: The idea of a childhood friend who she rekindles a love with, again, cheap story line that is WAAAAY over done, but okay, I can deal with it. But the idea that through this love that they share, that he would just get up and leave in the middle of the night to never be found again, only to learn that he has a rare brain cancer that is taking his life and that he doesn't want the even rarer brain surgery that could save him, and he vanishes out of thin air because he loves her too much to hurt her, made me want to hurl this book out my bedroom window like that scene from Silver Linings Playbook, because its so dumb. This is the same twisted logic men have been using on women to abandon them and still look like the good guy. "I left you high and dry because I was afraid of what I was feeling" No you're a self centered jerk. Please ladies, don't by this crap. If a man really wants to be with you, he'll be with you, hell or high water. Noah wrote Ali 365 letters, this dude can't even stick a post it on the door saying bye? The fact that Jennifer went rushing to his side, let alone even gave this douche the time of day after that makes her a doormat of a girlfriend, and if there is one thing I cannot stand is weak, spineless women in a story. Ugh. <br />And the Cancer card is over played. Did James Patterson have even one half original thought while writing this book? Cause I wasn't able to locate a single one. <br /><br />Three: Possibly my biggest problem with the entire book, DID ANYONE ELSE READ THE PART ABOUT HIM GIVING HER CAT CPR?! Did anyone else laugh actually audibly out loud like I did? <br />"Oh, you're cat electrocuted itself by chewing on some wires and has been lying here dead for only God knows how long, but let me wrap my mouth around his nose and blow and press on his side and BAM magic, cat is alive." <br />SMDH. <br />Just bad writing, as bad and awful as I've ever seen. The publishing company should be ashamed that they allowed that in print. <br /><br /><br />Blah Blah Blah, she talks him into getting the surgery (surprise) He lives (Damn it) they go on to happy ever after. Granny dies (probably cause you left her high and dry in the hospital you selfish person you) and whaddya know at the end of it all she announces she pregnant and there naming it after the Grandma (who had an affair on her husband, btw, best role model ever) and everyone cheers and happy days ensue. <br /><br />But you know, out of all the awful that this book is, I am thankful for it for one thing, I now I have something to stoke my fireplace with on snowy winter days. <br /><br />I sincerely hope Mr. Patterson's thriller/mystery stories are better than his love stories, because if they're not I'm quitting my job today, running off to New York and becoming a writer, because any half baked idea I write in my sleep will be better than this. <br /><br />I still want my penny back. <br /><br /> <br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8067100431210928699" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

When Sam falls into a coma, the narrator reads the letters, while getting entangled with a summer childhood pal Brendan Kellar, moved in nearby. He's handsome, kind, funny, so guess what's next? Too sickly sweet. I skipped faster and faster to hit the high points. <br /><br />When I saw Sam Gamgee, faithful hobbit companion to Frodo in Lord of the Rings, on the Goodreads character list, I reread the whole book in detail. Brendan's father (uncle) is Arthur p66 Andrew p277; Jen's cousin Eric p74 is Bobby p311. Maybe I'll pay more attention to fine print. (I have a personal anti-secret marriages bias from bad experiences.) <br /><br />Sam wakes from the coma. Brendan survives brain tumor surgery, which he'd declined until Jen came along. When he has recuperated, the younger couple meet Doc, the local Reverend, but three weeks later, Sam dies. At Sam's funeral, narrator announces baby Sam coming. Epilogue is video of 14 day old girl in their new home, no mention of marriage. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> </span>

<div id="review_113547952" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/113547952" />
    <a title="Drebbles" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1862888-drebbles"><img alt="Drebbles" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365895783p2/1862888.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/113547952?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Drebbles" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Drebbles" href="/user/show/1862888-drebbles">Drebbles</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1862888-drebbles?shelf=2007">2007</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer113547952" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14067693329297715458">Devastated after the tragic death of her husband, Jennifer has buried herself in working as a columnist for the Chicago Tribune. But when her beloved Grandmother, Samantha, has a bad fall and is in a coma, Jennifer drops everything to travel to Lake Geneva, an hour and a half away. Jennifer spent many wonderful summers at Lake Geneva as a child and despite the circumstances she's happy to be in one of her favorite places. While at the cottage, Jennifer discovers her grandmother has left her a pa</span>
  <span id="freeText14067693329297715458" style="display:none">Devastated after the tragic death of her husband, Jennifer has buried herself in working as a columnist for the Chicago Tribune. But when her beloved Grandmother, Samantha, has a bad fall and is in a coma, Jennifer drops everything to travel to Lake Geneva, an hour and a half away. Jennifer spent many wonderful summers at Lake Geneva as a child and despite the circumstances she's happy to be in one of her favorite places. While at the cottage, Jennifer discovers her grandmother has left her a packet of letters that will reveal some secrets from her grandmother's past. As Jennifer is slowly finding out the secrets about her grandparents, she is also discovering her feelings for Brendan, who is also staying at Lake Geneva. But Brendan has a secret of his own, a secret that threatens to keep him and Jennifer apart forever. <br /><br />"Sam's Letters to Jennifer" is what I call a perfect beach book. It's not too deep, has a touch of tragedy, yet it's a good love story (two love stories actually) and doesn't require a lot of thought. None of the characters are particularly deep - Jennifer is supposed to be a workaholic but outside of one column, we never see her working and she soon ditches her job without a qualm. Same with Brendan, while he had a compelling reason to quit his job, neither he nor Jennifer seems to worry about money. Since we mostly see Sam through her letters, it's hard to sympathize with her as a character and her romance left me a bit cold. However, Jennifer and Brendan's love story was much more engaging. There are some plot holes; I was never quite sure if Jennifer's father was dead or alive, her mother is mentioned but he never is. Brendan's secret is a bit too melodramatic and the outcome a bit unbelievable, but sweet. But again, this isn't the kind of book you want to think too much about, instead just read and enjoy. <br /><br />"Sam's Letters to Jennifer" is a light, fluffy read - perfect for the beach or a rainy afternoon. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14067693329297715458" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2605001111" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2605001111" />
    <a title=" Ananya thefoodandbooklife" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52660761-ananya-thefoodandbooklife"><img alt=" Ananya thefoodandbooklife" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1512540662p2/52660761.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2605001111?book_show_action=true">Nov 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Ananya thefoodandbooklife" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Ananya thefoodandbooklife" href="/user/show/52660761-ananya-thefoodandbooklife"> Ananya thefoodandbooklife</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780755305742" href="/book/show/1015014.Sam_s_Letters_to_Jennifer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52660761-ananya-thefoodandbooklife?shelf=book-i-own-physical-copy">book-i-own-physical-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52660761-ananya-thefoodandbooklife?shelf=book-i-own">book-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52660761-ananya-thefoodandbooklife?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2605001111" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12811207152148393465">A book that I've re-read more times than I can count. It is my go-to 'feel good' read.<br/>Jennifer is a Chicago based columnist who has sworn off love following the death of her husband 2 years ago. She says she is happy with her job and her two cats. Her only family is her Grandmother Sam. But everything falls to pieces when she receives word that Sam is in a coma. She rushes to her side and discovers that Sam has left a series of letters for Jennifer. Jennifer discovers the truth about Sam's life </span>
  <span id="freeText12811207152148393465" style="display:none">A book that I've re-read more times than I can count. It is my go-to 'feel good' read.<br />Jennifer is a Chicago based columnist who has sworn off love following the death of her husband 2 years ago. She says she is happy with her job and her two cats. Her only family is her Grandmother Sam. But everything falls to pieces when she receives word that Sam is in a coma. She rushes to her side and discovers that Sam has left a series of letters for Jennifer. Jennifer discovers the truth about Sam's life and her secret love life. But that's not all that Lake Geneva has to offer. It also has Brendan Keller. Brendan just wants a final summer of peace and fun but, what is finds is the love of his life. But its almost too late. <br />Everyone's used to James Patterson's mystery writing but it was a pleasant surprise to discover that he writes brilliant romance as well. As was to be expected from an author of his caliber, the story makes for a very moving reading. The characters are real and have faced challenges that many of us have had to deal with. Nothing is over the top. You fall in love with each one of them and you are rooting for them to find a happy ending. <br />Everyone has secrets in their lives that they never tell another soul. I loved the idea of the grandmother telling her real story to her favorite granddaughter through letters. The way Sam's story was relevant to Jennifer's life was beautiful to discover. Brendan is the ideal boyfriend. You cannot help but wish that there was someone like him in your life. I am in tears every time I read the book and that is the mark of a well-written story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12811207152148393465" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/988101321" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/988101321?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy" href="/user/show/257722-amy">Amy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer988101321" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15061547636377397393">I can handle sappy stories. Really, some of them are quite good. But this? Sigh. My mom recommended it and really enjoyed it but I have to say I was sincerely disappointed.<br/><br/>Although I enjoyed the descriptions of Sam's house and Lake Geneva, there were just too many tragic twists in this story for me to take it seriously. Here come the spoilers...Jennifer's first husband dies, and she loses their baby - and she believes it's all her fault because she couldn't leave work in time for the Hawaiian va</span>
  <span id="freeText15061547636377397393" style="display:none">I can handle sappy stories. Really, some of them are quite good. But this? Sigh. My mom recommended it and really enjoyed it but I have to say I was sincerely disappointed.<br /><br />Although I enjoyed the descriptions of Sam's house and Lake Geneva, there were just too many tragic twists in this story for me to take it seriously. Here come the spoilers...Jennifer's first husband dies, and she loses their baby - and she believes it's all her fault because she couldn't leave work in time for the Hawaiian vacation on which Danny died (which, by the way, was so contrived...if the author wanted to make her a widow, why not something basic, like a car accident in their home city of Chicago? Good grief!). Her beloved grandmother is in a coma and reveals in letters, shockingly, that she never loved Jennifer's grandfather, a man who she married after about five minutes and turned out to be an abusive, controlling jerk. When at long last Sam does find true love, she can't leave her marriage because her true love is a widower with young-ish kids and, well, it's just completely inconceivable that people ever get divorced and remarry and have blended families.<br /><br />Jennifer does fall in love again but, wait - he's got terminal cancer! Oh, Jennifer is also without both of her parents, who each have died, though we don't know how. Even one of Jennifer's cats - who we meet and are told are so important to her, but we don't really see for the rest of the story - has a brush with death. <br /><br />Too much. Far, far too much.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15061547636377397393" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/78464872?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Valerie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Valerie" href="/user/show/2322545-valerie">Valerie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78464872" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15098359430179712907">A friend lent me this book, so you really can't complain about a free book... but I will anyways :-)<br/><br/>In the prologue, it's established that the main character, Jennifer, had lost her young husband, Danny, in a swimming accident 18 months before. She laments that she mostly went through this grieving on her own, with the exception of support from two friends. One of those two friends was named ... Danny. Okay, four characters have been introduced and two have the same name? Not a Danny and a Danie</span>
  <span id="freeText15098359430179712907" style="display:none">A friend lent me this book, so you really can't complain about a free book... but I will anyways :-)<br /><br />In the prologue, it's established that the main character, Jennifer, had lost her young husband, Danny, in a swimming accident 18 months before. She laments that she mostly went through this grieving on her own, with the exception of support from two friends. One of those two friends was named ... Danny. Okay, four characters have been introduced and two have the same name? Not a Danny and a Daniel, but both Danny. I had to reread a few pages to make sure I had it all straight. This is fiction - pick unique names! Why couldn't the friend be called Bob? David? Charles? the good news is that the friend Danny was only mentioned in the prologue and never again.<br /><br />The book covers Jennifer's ability to love again and her mixed up emotions when she finds her self falling for a childhood friend that ... is dying. Oh, and her grandmother is in a coma, likely dying. Fortunately for Jennifer, her grandmother has left her a series of letters detailing her life, so it would all be written down. Of course, Jennifer learns secrets so shocking she isn't sure what to do with them, but eventually learns to accept her grandmother for the imperfect woman she was.<br /><br />The book was a bit sappy for my taste, but due to the way it was mostly presented in "letters" it was a very fast read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15098359430179712907" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer158404233" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer4711881501218969793">One star seems a little harsh, but two stars, too much. I really wanted to enjoy a light, quick, sweet read. Unfortunately, as the story progressed I found it rather uncomfortable. Too many tragic circumstances for one small novel. I was disturbed by the immorality in the book. Especially the romance of Jennifer's grandmother by another man other than her husband. I did not find the characters endearing, people of integrity. The revelation of who "Doc" really was (you'll understand if you read i</span>
  <span id="freeText4711881501218969793" style="display:none">One star seems a little harsh, but two stars, too much. I really wanted to enjoy a light, quick, sweet read. Unfortunately, as the story progressed I found it rather uncomfortable. Too many tragic circumstances for one small novel. I was disturbed by the immorality in the book. Especially the romance of Jennifer's grandmother by another man other than her husband. I did not find the characters endearing, people of integrity. The revelation of who "Doc" really was (you'll understand if you read it) left me cold. There is no moral compass for these people, least of all Doc, which I found rather disconcerting. The writing was passable, what you would expect in a weepy romance novel. Just didn't touch my heart like other books have. <br />After you read this make a list of all the "tearjerk " moments and situations in this book. I'll start:<br />Young widow who has had a miscarrige, and blames self for husbands death..<br />Beloved grandmother in a coma in hospital.. Letters found for grandaughter to read of her past love life.. Handsome summer new love reveals a startling health secret.. and so on....<br /> </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer41663721&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer41663721" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer301373057650396484">So at first, I was a little surprised at the beginning that the book is written from a woman's point of view (Jennifer) -- not as a narration, but first-person -- and it's written by a man. But I quickly forgot that and started enjoying it. It's a touching summer romance story, and I enjoyed it more because it's set in a place I've been -- Lake Geneva, Wisconsin. I could actually picture it as the book unfolded, and remembered a beautiful Sunday morning my husband and I spent there one summer, s</span>
  <span id="freeText301373057650396484" style="display:none">So at first, I was a little surprised at the beginning that the book is written from a woman's point of view (Jennifer) -- not as a narration, but first-person -- and it's written by a man. But I quickly forgot that and started enjoying it. It's a touching summer romance story, and I enjoyed it more because it's set in a place I've been -- Lake Geneva, Wisconsin. I could actually picture it as the book unfolded, and remembered a beautiful Sunday morning my husband and I spent there one summer, sitting outside at Starbucks.<br /><br />I'm not positive if the information below would be considered a spoiler or not, but I don't want to ruin it for anyone, so: Spoiler Alert: <br />Sam is actually Jennifer's grandmother, who is basically in a coma for the majority of the book. Jennifer, who lives in Chicago, rushes up to Lake Geneva to be with her grandmother and ends up staying for most of the summer. She reads a few letters at a time, letters that her grandmother wrote to tell her about her life.<br /><br />This was a very sweet book to read, and just right for <i>my</i> summer!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13449698191607517321">This book was a bit of a shocker after reading quite a few books by Christian authors that kept their books very clean. Her husband drowned on a vacation in Hawaii, and she blames herself for it because she made some changes in their initial plans. She has a very close </span>
  <span id="freeText13449698191607517321" style="display:none">This book was a bit of a shocker after reading quite a few books by Christian authors that kept their books very clean. There were a few swear words, and some of the subject matter was treated so lightly that it was a bit disturbing. <br /><br />It was a very fast read, and is the story about a 30 something newspaper columnist that lives a pretty lonely life. Her husband drowned on a vacation in Hawaii, and she blames herself for it because she made some changes in their initial plans. She has a very close relationship with her grandmother, Sam, and early in the story she receives a phone call that Sam is in the hospital in a coma. She heads to the lakeside town, and finds a bunch of letters to her from her grandma. She'd asked for years to hear her grandma's story, and the letters tell Sam's story. Throughout Jennifer's stay, she reads these letters. It is shocking to her in the first one to read that her grandma never loved her grandpa. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13449698191607517321" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_42563437" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/42563437" />
    <a title="Kristy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2450583-kristy"><img alt="Kristy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1301017941p2/2450583.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/42563437?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristy" href="/user/show/2450583-kristy">Kristy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780446615426" href="/book/show/1055595.Sam_s_Letter_to_Jennifer">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer42563437" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer760285021823605518">This book revives memories for me of my own past, and my own relationship with my grandmother. I was pleasantly surprised that the story is composed into letters every few chapters. It reminds me a little of The Color Purple. This book offers plenty of closure, and it ends how it should. There are surprises, tragedy, and lessons to be learned. The most important lesson: Don't take life for granted, live each day as if it were your last. </span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_143651178" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/143651178" />
    <a title="Alicen Dub" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3973522-alicen-dub"><img alt="Alicen Dub" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1303008910p2/3973522.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/143651178?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alicen Dub" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alicen Dub" href="/user/show/3973522-alicen-dub">Alicen Dub</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780759511163" href="/book/show/9939799-sam-s-letters-to-jennifer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3973522-alicen-dub?shelf=just-because">just-because</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer143651178" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7150227676948946392">I really enjoyed this book. It made me laugh it made me cry and I fell in love with Sam. She was such an incredible woman. Reading this book I could feel the love she had for her granddaughter and for the love of her life. I was happy but not really surprised to hear who it was she fell in love with mostly cause all books like this have a predictability about them. I am not usually a mushy love story kind of person but I really enjoy the ones that James Patterson writes.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_1010434949" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1010434949" />
    <a title="Kris - My Novelesque Life" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6275022-kris---my-novelesque-life"><img alt="Kris - My Novelesque Life" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577743166p2/6275022.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1010434949?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kris - My Novelesque Life" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kris - My Novelesque Life" href="/user/show/6275022-kris---my-novelesque-life">Kris - My Novelesque Life</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1010434949" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6935766825785975003">ZERO STARS<br/><br/>"Grief-stricken by a recent tragedy, Jennifer returns to the resort village where she grew up to help her beloved grandmother. There, Jennifer will discover new meaning in life and experience not one, but two of the most amazing love stories ever." (From Amazon)<br/><br/>Patterson is trying to channel Nicholas Sparks but it comes off as a very watered down A Message in a Bottle.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne  (Booklady) Molinarolo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne  (Booklady) Molinarolo" href="/user/show/3615945-anne-booklady-molinarolo">Anne  (Booklady) Molinarolo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3615945-anne-booklady-molinarolo?shelf=permanent-library">permanent-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3615945-anne-booklady-molinarolo?shelf=good-fiction">good-fiction</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer806912450" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7457095125669774026">What a beautiful, heartwarming story about a grandmother and her secret love and her granddaughter, Jennifer, who has experienced so much loss in a short period of time. Sam's letters to Jennifer had me in tears and smiles as I read Sam's story. Yes, Love never dies.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('o1zCkTuhsnsjeWgeWnfi+n83RaUMoICDFakN896N0UQqvc3Ujpmm9HZl8WV2rFKOnv5Am6xnSlvkK/ktZCjx5A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gp2J9h8VhZcty56hwbcel2wsSWhjaBA/Kc1sUKCleKoLfIazqi2RGHjXB9rtbK7jjeVMVsOv2ufYT5iOGgBYCg==')})
  }

He has created more enduring fictional characters than any other novelist writing today, with his Alex Cross, Michael Bennett, Women’s Murder Club, Private, NYPD Red, Daniel X, Maximum Ride, and Middle School series. He has sold over 380 million books wo</span>
  <span id="freeText8542961696260308600" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.jamespatterson.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Official US Site</a><br /><a href="http://www.jamespatterson.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Official UK Site</a><br /><a href="http://jimmypatterson.org" rel="nofollow noopener">JIMMY Patterson Books</a><br /><a href="http://readkiddoread.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">ReadKiddoRead</a><br /><br /><br /><br />James Patterson is the world’s bestselling author and most trusted storyteller. He has created more enduring fictional characters than any other novelist writing today, with his Alex Cross, Michael Bennett, Women’s Murder Club, Private, NYPD Red, Daniel X, Maximum Ride, and Middle School series. He has sold over 380 million books worldwide and currently holds the Guinness World Record for the most #1 New York Times bestsellers. In addition to writing the thriller novels for which he is best known, among them The President Is Missing with President Bill Clinton, Patterson also writes fiction for young readers of all ages, including the Max Einstein series, produced in partnership with the Albert Einstein Estate. He is also the first author to have #1 new titles simultaneously on the New York Times adult and children’s bestseller lists.<br /> <br />The son of an insurance salesman and a schoolteacher, Patterson grew up in Newburgh, New York, and began casually writing at the age of nineteen. In 1969, he graduated from Manhattan College. He was given a full-ride scholarship to Vanderbilt University’s graduate program in English. He left Vanderbilt before getting his PhD due to complications involving the Vietnam War. <br /> <br />Instead, he moved to New York to become a junior copywriter for the advertising agency J. Walter Thompson, eventually becoming CEO of its North American company.<br /> <br />In 1976, while still working for J. Walter Thompson, Patterson published his first novel, The Thomas Berryman Number, with Little, Brown and Company. After being turned down by thirty-one publishers, it won the Edgar Award for Best First Novel. Patterson’s 1993 novel, Along Came a Spider, his first book to feature Alex Cross, was also his first New York Times bestseller in fiction.<br /> <br />In 2001, Morgan Freeman starred as Alex Cross in a film adaptation of Along Came a Spider, and Tyler Perry also played the character in the 2012 film Alex Cross. A film adaptation of Patterson’s middle-grade novel Middle School: The Worst Years of My Life was released in theaters in October 2016.<br /> <br />James Patterson has donated more than one million books to students, focusing on some of the most under-resourced schools and youth programs in the country. To date, he has donated $7.25 million to school and classroom libraries throughout the United States, and $2.1 million to independent bookstores and employees.<br /> <br />Patterson has recently donated over $35 million to his and his wife’s alma maters—the University of Wisconsin, Vanderbilt University, and Manhattan College—and he has established over four hundred Teacher and Writer Education Scholarships at twenty-one colleges and universities throughout the country. Patterson has also donated more than one million books to U.S. soldiers at home and overseas.<br /> <br />In May 2015, Patterson launched a children’s book imprint at Little, Brown—JIMMY Patterson—that is unwaveringly focused on one goal: turning kids into lifelong readers. This imprint also provides resources, strategies, and programs to serve teachers, parents, librarians, and booksellers. Patterson invests proceeds from the sales of JIMMY Patterson Books in pro-reading initiatives.<br /> <br />Patterson also founded ReadKiddoRead.com, a website designed to help parents, teachers, and librarians ignite a new generation’s excitement for reading. Awarded the National Book Foundation’s Innovations in Reading Prize and the American Library Association’s Great Websites for Kids, the site features thoughtful book reviews from a variety of genres and age ranges, a large and lively Facebook community, and contributions from other authors.<br /> <br />Patterson’s awards for adult and children’s literature include the Edgar Award, the International </span>
  <a data-text-id="8542961696260308600" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
